O-RAN.WG1.Use-Cases-Detailed-Specification-R003-v10.00 
This sub-use case  includes the configuration of multi -operator role -based access control (configuration) for the 1 
management sessions associated with a tenant operator. The shared O -RU uses the PLMN -Id associated with the 2 
management account and used in other asp ects of the shared O -RU’s configuration to prevent a tenant from reading 3 
configuration associated with a second tenant’s partitioned resources or subscribing to performance measurements 4 
associated with a second tenant’s partitioned resources. 5 
This sub -use case also describes the procedures of how a sharing co -ordinator can confirm that a tenant operator is 6 
complying with the sharing agreements that cover operation of a shared O-RU. 7 
The outcome is that the shared O-RU has been configured with the configuration parameters necessary for operation.  8 
3.20.1.5 Supervision use case of a shared O-RU 9 
This sub use case applies to the running / operation of Shared O-RU. 10 
This sub use case describes the supervision operations of the Shared O-RU. This sub use case is triggered after the O-11 
DUs have configured the partitioned carrier information of a shared O-RU. It is invoked during run-time. The actors are 12 
the SMO, O-DUs, and shared O-RU. The objective that the use case accomplishes is the establishment of watchdog 13 
supervision of the shared O-RU by multiple O-DUs. Supervision enables the shared O-RU to autonomously cease 14 
transmitting on a partitioned carrier if it loses supervision with the O-DU responsible for that carrier. 15 
3.20.1.6 Performance Management use case of a shared O-RU  16 
This sub use case applies to the running / operation of Shared O-RU. 17 
This sub use case describes the performance management operations of the Shared O -RU. This sub use case is triggered 18 
after the O-DUs have configured the partitioned carrier information of a shared O-RU. It is invoked during run-time. 19 
The actors are the O-DUs, and shared O-RU. The objective that the use case accomplishes is for each O-DU to establish 20 
subscriptions to receive performance management notifications regarding operation  of the fronthaul between the O-DUs 21 
and shared O-RU.  22 
3.20.1.7 Antenna Line Device (ALD) control use case of a shared O-RU  23 
This sub use case applies to the running / operation of Shared O-RU. 24 
This sub use case describes the operation of antenna line devices with the Shared O -RU. This sub use case is triggered 25 
after the O-DUs have configured the partitioned carrier information of a shared O -RU. The actors are one of the O-DUs, 26 
and shared O-RU. The objective that the use case accomplishes is for the selected O -DU to operate the ALD controller 27 
and control the ALD connected to the shared O-RU.  28 
ALD control is an end-to-end operation from the operator using the SMO at one end issuing operations to the O-DU and 29 
realising that ALD operation through the O-RU on through to the terminating ALD device at the other end. 30 
Because there is a single ALD controller, and the shared O -RU can be connected to multiple O -DUs, one of them needs 31 
to be nominated as the ALD controller. 32 
There are many types of operations for ALD control. These include but not limited to software update of ALD devices, 33 
setting of RET mechanical/electrical tilt setting, Reset of ALD devices, etc.  34

3.20.1.8 Resiliency use case of a shared O-RU 1 
This sub use case describes system recovery from failures of various combinations during one or more O -DUs for a 2 
Shared O-RU. The actors are the SMO, O -DUs and Shared O -RU. The actors work together to recover operation or 3 
maintain operation for failures of O-DUs.  4 
The resiliency sub use case covers various aspects of a Shared O-RU that is undergoing maintenance, or different elements 5 
(O-DU, or Shared O-RU) have failed. For example, if a [Primary/host] O-DU connectivity has failed, this use case overs 6 
a flow of operations that occur when a shared O-DU has failed.  7 
This use case is triggered through different situations when a the [primary/host] O -DU fails or is deliberately removed 8 
from service. For example, during a maintenance situation, where in a servic e provider’s maintenance window the 9 
[primary/host] O-DU is taken out of service for maintenance. 10 
Considerations include startup with the [secondary] O -DU. The [secondary] O-DU becoming the new [primary/host] O-11 
DU, transient failure and consequent quick recovery of the [primary/host] O-DU. 12 
3.20.1.9 Antenna calibration use case of a shared O-RU (deferred)  13 
This sub use case applies to the running / operation of Shared O-RU. 14 
This sub use case describes the operation of antenna calibration using a Shared O-RU. This sub use case is triggered after 15 
the O-DUs have configured the partitioned carrier information of a shared O -RU. The actors are the O -DUs, and shared 16 
O-RU. The objective that the use case accomplishes is for the shared O -RU to be able to perform antenn a calibration 17 
when connected to multiple O-DUs.  18 
3.20.1.10 Rehoming use case of a shared O-RU (deferred) 19 
This sub use case describes how a Shared O -RU is moved within a network and paired with new O -DUs. This might be 20 
a virtual rehoming in a cloud native deployment, or a physical move. 21 
This is typically done with replanning of a network, or rolling a new of an existing deploying (greenfield pocket in a 22 
brownfield network), moving tiger sites into a network. 23

3.20.1.11 Reset use case of a shared O-RU  28 
The reset of a Shared O -RU sub-use case describes the o perations related to taking a Shared O -RU out of service  and 29 
resetting it. 30 
There are some important aspects to reset of Shared O -RU. Only the Shared O -RU Host would have permissions to 31 
perform the reset operation.  32 
In a multiple MNO configuration, reset operations would need to be coordinated between operators. The Shared O -RU 33 
Host operator has the permission to perform the reset of a Shared O -RU. It would expect that the Shared O -RU Host 34 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
© 2023 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the copyright statement on the cover page of this specification.         131 
O-RAN.WG1.Use-Cases-Detailed-Specification-R003-v10.00 
operator would try to coordinate with the Shared Resource Operator (SRO). This may entail something as simple as those 1 
two operators talking to each other; it may also entail automated coordination between management entities of these 2 
operators. The reset of a Shared O-RU would impact availability, reliability, and maintenance (ARM) metrics, and uptime 3 
KPIs. 4 
The reset of a Shared O-RU operation is the basis for maintenance activities, debugging operations, the physically moving, 5 
physical rehoming, and recovery from malfunctions of the Shared O-RU.  6 
There are situations where the Shared O-RU would autonomously reset itself. When the Shared O -RU has lost M-Plane 7 
connectivity to all of its connected O-DUs the Shared O-RU would autonomously reset itself. This would be the same as 8 
if the O-RU was not in a shared configuration. 9 
A software update will result in a reset of the Shared O -RU. The software update of a Shared O -RU is expected to be 10 
coordinated between the Shared O-RU Host and the SRO. 11 
Before removing the Shared O-RU from service, the Shared O-RU carriers and its associated cells on O-DU/O-CU should 12 
be deactivated.  13 
3.20.1.12 Advanced Resiliency Sub-use cases of a shared O-RU 14 
Advanced Resiliency Sub Use Cases describes other more intricate interactions and response for Resiliency operations.  15 
3.20.1.13 Load-balancing Sub-use case of a shared O-RU 16 
Load-balancing is a use case where relevant actors can reallocate Share O -RU resources based on triggers, metrics, or 17 
policies. 18 
A key actor is a policy -enforcer that makes Shared O -RU resource allocation decisions based on inp uts from 19 
measurements. For example, measurements may indicate the amount of traffic on each of the two O -DUs connected to 20 
the shared O-RU. The policy-enforcer decides when a reallocation of Shared O -RU resources is needed. For example, if 21 
the policy-enforcer observes that one O-DU has a disproportionate amount of traffic (e.g., more users per MHz) than the 22 
other O-DU, the policy-enforcer makes a decision to re-allocate a component carrier from one O-DU to the other O-DUs.   23 
The policy-enforcer role could be played by the SMO/Non-RT RIC or the near-RT RIC, depending on the time granularity 24 
of load balancing decision -making needed. There are limitations that are governed from the air interface which will 25 
influence the mechanisms and time granularity for load balancing. Policies can reflect a variety of triggers or mechanisms 26 
to be used to balance traffic or carriers. These might include guaranteed bandwidth, O -DU computational load/capacity 27 
(processor occupancy), and time of day triggers among others. Whatever the policy rules are and how often they are 28 
evaluated, the policy -enforcer would evaluate the situation, probably periodically, and make a resource re -allocation 29 
decision. 30

3.20.3 Solution 1 
3.20.3.1 General aspects of solutions for all shared O-RU use cases 2 
The following sections describe solutions that apply to each of the sub –Use Cases. They describe different solutions for 3 
key aspects of Shared O -RU operation, such as the Start -up, configuration, supervision, and performance management 4 
among other things. There are a f ew general aspects of each of these solutions that share similar goals, assumptions, 5 
actors, and roles.  6 
 7 
Use Case Stage Evolution / Specification <<Uses>> 
Related use 
Common Goals  
 
All the following sub -use cases involve either getting the Shared O -RU 
operational or keeping it operational. Each of the sub -use cases explore a 
different aspect of these two common goals. Each of the sub-use cases has a 
different specific goal and is trying to accomplish a particular dimension of 
Shared O-RU operation. 
Bringing into operation – Many of the sub-Use Cases have the goal to get 
the Shared O-RU operational and capable of supporting over the air traffic. 
These include the resource partitioning, start -up, configuration, and 
supervision sub-use cases. They are “day 0” related use cases. 
Maintaining Service  – The other set of sub -use cases are related to 
maintaining service. These include the supervision, performance, and 
resiliency sub-use cases. These use cases relate to the continued operation of 
the Shared O-RU, thus “day 2” operation. 
 
Common Actors  
 
The Shared O -RU and the multiple O -DUs that the Shared O -RU is 
connected to are common actors that apply to all the following sub –Use 
Cases. 
The common configurations that apply to the sub -Use Cases many also 
involve the management system between two operators. 
Some actors can be controlled by different operators and / or provided by 
different solution providers. 
 
Common 
Assumptions  
 
For the following sub-use cases it is assumed that a ll relevant functions and 
components are instantiated. 
Inventory management systems identify shared O -RU and the available O-
DUs as inventory elements. 
For all of the sub -use cases, an O -RU resources are statically partitioned 
between O-DUs (static configuration) 
 
 8 
All the sub -use cases also apply a set of common configurations. These sub use cases are intended to apply to Single 9 
Operator (MNO) and Multiple Operator (MNO) configurations. The configurations will be important to service providers, 10 
wireless operators as they roll out new networks. Those configurations can then be further broken down into either Hybrid 11 
or Hierarchical configurations. In a Hierarchical configuration the SMO performs configuration and FCAPS/LCM with 12 
the O-DU which in does that for the O -RUs. In a Hybrid configuration, the SMO can perform operations with either the 13 
O-DU and/or the O -RU. The O -DUs that share the O -RU can be from either common or different vendors. It can be 14 
envisaged that many more possible configurations or variations of those basic configu rations could be supported by the 15 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
© 2023 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the copyright statement on the cover page of this specification.         137 
O-RAN.WG1.Use-Cases-Detailed-Specification-R003-v10.00 
following Sub-Use Cases. For example, more than just two O -DUs. Sub-use cases present solutions that are intended to 1 
apply to all these possible configurations. Exceptions may arise from the variations of the Resiliency su b-use case.  2 
The collection of the sub -use cases either bring a Shared O -RU into operation by performing vital aspects of getting a 3 
shared O-RU initially working; or they try to keep a Shared O -RU operational. Additionally, these sub-Use Cases apply 4 
to some other use cases such as class 2 BBU pooling ( BBU Pooling to achieve RAN Elasticity  use case), RAN Sharing, 5 
and advanced multi -vendor multi -operator Network Slicing operation ( Multi-vendor Slices ). Support for different 6 
configuration, resiliency operation and, supervision that apply to Shared O-RU will often be relevant to these other related 7 
Use Cases as well. These other related use cases can use the following sub-use cases as building blocks operations because 8 
they provide basic goals and objectives to getting a shared O-RU operational and keeping it running. Thus, the sub -Use 9 
Cases are likely be applicable to many those use cases outside of just this Shared O -RU Use Case.  10

3.20.3.3 Start-up use case of shared O-RU 27 
The following describes the solution for the start-up sub use case for a Shared O-RU. 28 


 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
© 2023 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the copyright statement on the cover page of this specification.         139 
O-RAN.WG1.Use-Cases-Detailed-Specification-R003-v10.00 
Use Case Stage Evolution / Specification <<Uses>> 
Related use  
Goal 
The shared O-RU is operating with the necessary software version and 
has established network connectivity with the O -DU(s) and, for hybrid 
deployments, the SMO 
 
Actors and 
Roles 
Shared O-RU calls home and establishes network management session. 
SMO is responsible for software management for the shared O-RU when 
operating in hybrid management mode 
O-DU is responsible for software management for the shared O-RU when 
operating in hierarchical management mode  
 
Assumptions None  
Begins when Shared O-RU powers on  
Preconditions Transport systems (DHCP server) has been configured with call home 
configuration information  
Step 1 (M) 
ESTABLISH SYNCHRONISATION: 
 
Each O -DU and Shared O -RU establish synchronisation with a timing 
source, for example PTP (IEEE 1588) or Sync-E.  
 
Note #1: It is expected the O-RU and all O-DUs connected it would share 
the same synchronisation source otherwise, the O-DUs will drift in timing. 
Note #2: For more details on O-RU sync and O-RU loss of sync, see the 
M-Plane specification clause 15.3.3: Carrier state’s relationship to 
synchronisation state. 
 
 
Step 2 (M) 
SYNCHRONISATION STATE CHANGE NOTIFICATION: 
 
After the O-RU has a synchronisation source, all subscribed O-DU(s) are 
notified through a Synchronisation State Change Notification. We expect 
the O-RU to be in the sync state “LOCKED”. 
 
The Synchronisation State Change Notification goes from Shared O -RU 
to all subscribed O-DU(s).  
 
It is possible that the synchronisation procedure can happen in parallel to 
the other steps of the start -up sub-use case. Thus, many of the other 
steps in th is use case can happen as the synchronization procedure 
occurs. Even though this is shown as “step 2” this may complete after 
other steps. 
 
 
Step 3 (ALT) 
[Shared O-RU operated in hybrid management mode] 
Shared O -RU calls home and triggers establishment of  network 
management session with SMO 
ORAN-
WG4.MP.0 
Clause 6.3 
and/or Clause 
6.9.2 
Step 4 (ALT) 
[Shared O-RU operated in hierarchical management mode] 
Shared O -RU calls home and triggers establishment of network 
management session with O-DU#1 
ORAN-
WG4.MP.0 
Clause 6.3 
Step 5 (ALT) 
[Shared O-RU operated in hierarchical management mode] 
Shared O -RU calls home and triggers establishment of network 
management session with O-DU#2 
ORAN-
WG4.MP.0 
Clause 6.3

[Shared O-RU operated in hybrid management mode] 
SMO recovers software inventory 
ORAN-

[Shared O -RU operated in hybrid management mode and software 
update required] 
SMO triggers download of new software 
ORAN-
WG4.MP.0 
Clause 8.5

________________________________________________________________________________________________

O-RAN.WG1.Use-Cases-Detailed-Specification-R003-v10.00 
Use Case Stage Evolution / Specification <<Uses>> 
Related use  
Goal The shared O-RU is configured to operate with multiple o-DUs  
Actors and 
Roles 
SMO responsible for shared O-RU common configuration when 
operating in hybrid management mode 
SMO optionally can subscribe to receive notifications of modifications to 
shared O-RU’s configuration 
When operating in hierarchical management mode, rApp is responsible 
for determining whi ch O -DU is responsible for common configuration 
aspects 
Shared O-RU responsible for role based accessccontrol based on PLMN-
Id 
O-DU is responsible for shared O-RU carrier configuration and optionally, 
when operating in hierarchical management mode, the sha red O -RU 
common configuration 
Sharing co -ordinator can check the shared O-RU’s committed 
configuration complies with any sharing agreement  
 
Assumptions None  
Begins when Shared O -RU has started up and has been configured with correct 
software version  
Preconditions None  
Step 1 (O) 
[Shared O-RU operated in hierarchical management mode] 
rApp determines which O-DU is responsible for common configuration of 
shared O-RU  
 
Step 2 (M) rApp triggers the configuration of the common aspects of the shared O -
RU  
Step 3 (M) Non-RT RIC triggers the configuration of the common aspects of the 
shared O-RU  
Step 4 (ALT) 
[Hybrid or neutral host management mode] 
SMO uses OpenFronthaul interface to configure common aspects of 
shared O-RU 
ORAN-
WG4.MP.0 
Clause 9 
Step 5 (ALT) 
[Hierarchical management mode] 
SMO uses O1 interface to configure shared O-RU’s common aspects via 
O-DU 
 
Step 6 (ALT) 
[Hierarchical management mode] 
O-DU uses OpenFronthaul interface to configure common aspects of 
shared O-RU 
ORAN-
WG4.MP.0 
Clause 9 
Step 7 (O) Shared O_RU calls home to tenant’s O-DU (multi-operator)  
Step 8 (O) Shared O-RU calls home to tenant’s SMO (multi-operator)  
Step 9 (O) rApp triggers the configuration of the carrier aspects of the shared O-RU 
(non-neutral host)  
Step 10 (O) Non-RT RIC triggers the configuration of the carrier aspects of the shared 
O-RU  
Step 11 (O) SMO configures O-DU#1 and partitioned carrier information #1  
Step 12 (O) 
O-DU#1 configures partitioned carrier information #1 on shared O -RU 
non-neutral host) 
ORAN-
WG4.MP.0 
Clause 9 
Step 13( O) Tenant’s SMO configures O-DU#2 and partitioned carrier information #2 
(multi-operator)  
Step 14 (M) 
O-DU#2 configures partitioned carrier information #2 on shared O-RU ORAN-
WG4.MP.0 
Clause 9 
Step 15 (O) Shared O-RU implements role-based access control based oplmn-id#2  
Step 16 (O) 
The shared O-RU notifies SMO of its modified configuration ORAN-
WG4.MP.0 
Clause 9.4 
Step 17 (O) SMO signals Non -RT RIC information pertaining to changed 
configuration  
Step 18 (O) Non-RT RIC signals changed configuration to shared O -RU 
Orchestration rApp   
Step 19 (O) Sharing co-ordinator checks that the changed configuration compliance 
with the sharing agreement  
Step 20 (O) Host sharing co -ordinator indicates non -compliance with tenant sharing 
co-ordinator and remedial actions agreed (out of band exchange)  
Ends when  The shared O -RU is configured with common aspects and partitioned 
carrier#1 for O-DU#1 and partitioned carrier #2 for O-DU#2

3.20.3.5 Supervision use case of a shared O-RU 3 
The following describes the solution for the supervision sub use case for a Shared O-RU. 4 


 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
© 2023 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the copyright statement on the cover page of this specification.         148 
O-RAN.WG1.Use-Cases-Detailed-Specification-R003-v10.00 
Use Case Stage Evolution / Specification <<Uses>> 
Related use  
Goal 
The shared O-RU operates watchdog timers with each of its O-DUs and 
ceases transmitting on a partitioned carrier associated with an O-DU if is 
watchdog timer to that O-DU expires. 
 
Actors and 
Roles 
Shared O -RU operates watchdog timers and deactivates any carriers 
associated with an expired watchdog timer 
O-DU repeatedly resets the shared O-RU’s supervision timer  
SMO forwards any alarms to shared O-RU rApp 
 
Assumptions 
O-DUs are operating fronthaul control and user plane for their respective 
partitioned carriers 
SMO has subscribed to receive alarm notifications (hybrid management 
model) 
 
Begins when An O-DU subscribes to receive supervision notifications  
Step 1 (Loop) O-DU#1 performs supervision operations   
Step 2 (O) Shared O -RU detects supervision failure with O -DU#1 and ceases 
transmitting on partitioned carrier associated with O-DU  
Step 3 (O) Shared O-RU sends alarm notification to Fault Management   
Step 4 (O) Fault management sends alarm notification to Non-RT RIC  
Step 5 (O) Non-RT RIC sends alarm notification to shared o-RU Orchestration rApp  
Step 6 (Loop) O-DU#2 performs supervision operations   
Step 7 (O) Shared O -RU detects supervision failure with O -DU#2 and ceases 
transmitting on partitioned carrier associated with O-DU  
Step 8 (O) Shared O-RU sends alarm notification to Fault Management   
Step 9 (O) Fault management sends alarm notification to Non-RT RIC  
Step 10 (O) Non-RT RIC sends alarm notification to shared O-RU Orchestration rApp  
Ends when O-DU terminates subscription to supervision notification   
Exceptions None identified.  
Post Conditions None identified

________________________________________________________________________________________________

Use Case Stage Evolution / Specification <<Uses>> 
Related use  
Goal

management notifications regarding operation of the fronthaul between 
the O-DUs and shared O-RU. 
 
Actors and 
Roles

partitioned carrier basis

shared O-RU

partitioned carrier

shared O-Ru

Step 2 (M) ODU#2 subscribes to receive PM notifications from shared O-RU  
Step 3 (loop) Shared O-RU sends PM Notification to O-DU#1  
Step 4 (loop) Shared O-RU sends PM Notification to O-DU#2

3.20.3.7 Antenna Line device (ALD) control use case of a shared O-RU 14 
The following describes the solution for the ALD control sub use case for a Shared O-RU. 15 


 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
© 2023 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the copyright statement on the cover page of this specification.         153 
O-RAN.WG1.Use-Cases-Detailed-Specification-R003-v10.00 
Use Case Stage Evolution / Specification <<Uses>> 
Related use  
Goal The ALD connected to shared O -RU is configured to operate with ALD 
Controller  
Actors and 
Roles 
rApp is responsible for determining which O -DU is responsible for ALD 
Controller aspects 
O-DU is responsible for implementing ALD Controller 
O-RU is responsible for bridging between OFH and HDLC 
ALD is responsible for terminating HDLC  
 
Assumptions None  
Begins when Shared O -RU has started up and has been configured with correct 
software version  
Preconditions None  
Step 1 (M) rApp determines which O -DU is responsible for performing ALD 
Controller functionality

Step 4 (M) SMO uses O1 interface to configure ALD Controller in O-DU   
Step 5 (M) 
O-DU uses OpenFronthaul interface to configure ALD aspects of shared 
O-RU

3.20.3.8 Resiliency use case of a shared O-RU 1 
The following describes the solution for the Resiliency sub use case for a Shared O-RU. 2 
Use Case Stage Evolution / Specification <<Uses>> 
Related use  
Goal 
The goal of this sub use case is to handle situations related to resiliency 
operations with the Shared O-RU. For example, during maintenance the 
host O-DU has removed from service, and how the system can keep the 
Shared O-RU operational in this maintenance operation. 
 
This is a service impacting use case. 
 
Actors and 
Roles 
Shared O-RU 
The associations and control of the Shared O -RU is affected O -
DUs.  
O-DUs (Host/Tenant/ &other O-DUs) 
All the O -DUs connected to the Shared O -RU are actors  that are 
relevant in some way during a resiliency operation. 
SMO: 
The SMO makes high -level decisions related failures and the 
various resiliency situations.  
 
Assumptions 
It is assumed that there is always at least one O-DU still operational with 
the Shared O-RU. 
It is assumed that the resiliency operations are intended to maintain as 
much operational service for the Shared O-RU as possible  
 
Begins when 
There are many possible operations that trigger the resiliency use case. 
 
The purpose of the Resil iency use case is to keep the Shared O -RU 
operational in the face of a failure of the active O -DU. There are many 
possible situations where the active O -DU fails or is purposefully 
removed from operation which are all triggers for this use case. 
 
For example, in a case where a O-DU is taken out of service, it might be 
intentionally removed, or physically removed. Maintenance, software 
upgrade, network failure, power outages, communication links down are 
just some of the many possible situations where the ac tive O -DU is 
removed from operation. 
 
Preconditions 
The shared O -RU has connectivity to one or more O -DUs (and one of 
them is serving the primary role) 
The Shared O-DU has been configured originally by the active O-DU, and 
also carriers for the standby O-DUs. 
 
CU Plane Monitoring has been properly configured which sets up a 
communication monitoring interval for the interface between the shared 
O-RU and O-DU. 
 
O-DUs have subscribed to alarm notifications successfully. 
 
Step 1 (M) CONFIGURE ODU#1 FOR ACTIVE OPERATION 
  
Step 2 (M) CONFIGURE ODU#2 FOR STANDBY OPERATION  
Step 3 (M) 
ACTIVE O-DU FAILS 
Active O -DU (the one serving as the primary role) is no longer 
operational. The Shared O -RU loses communication with the active O -
DU. 
 
Note: the active O -DU may  be no longer operational for a variety of 
reasons. (see the “Begins when” section) 
 
 
Step 4.1 (ALT) M-PLANE MONITORING  
  

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
© 2023 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the copyright statement on the cover page of this specification.         156 
O-RAN.WG1.Use-Cases-Detailed-Specification-R003-v10.00 
In the Shared O -RU, when M -Plane OAM Monitoring interval timer 
triggers, the Shared O-RU will detect that is has lost OAM communication 
to the Active O-DU. 
 
Step 4.2 (ALT) Carriers Associated with that M-Plane connection are disabled.  
Step 4.3 (ALT) 
O-RU RAISES ALARMS TO SUBSCRIBERS 
 
The Shared O -RU raises the M -Plane loss connectivity alarm to 
Subscriber(s). The simple case shows that the O-DU#1 and O-DU#2 are 
subscribers. 
 
Step 4.4 (ALT) 
O-RU RAISES ALARMS TO SUBSCRIBERS 
 
The Shared O -RU raises the M -Plane loss connectivity alarm to 
Subscriber(s). The simple case shows that the O-DU#1 and O-DU#2 are 
subscribers. The Shared O-RU Raises an alarm to subscribers (O-DUs) 
that are still active, connected and subscribed. 
 
 
Step 4.5 (ALT) 
ALARM FORWARDED 
 
The Shared O-RU alarm is forwarded to the managing entity, such as the 
SMO. It is possible that the SMO will make the dec ision for making the 
standby O-DU#2 into the active O-DU.  
 
Note: There are many possible variations of this use case, where the 
SMO directly makes the decision of whether to make a standby O -DU 
into an active O-DU. This may happen even without a failure. These will 
be documented in other Sub-use cases. 
 
 
Step 4.6 (ALT) 
MANAGEMENT SYSTEM MAKES STANDBY ODU ACTIVE 
 
The Management system, SMO makes the standby O -DU#2 now 
becomes the active O-DU for the Shared O -RU. The message from the 
management system, SMO is sent to operational O-DU. 
 
Note: There might be multiple standby O-DUs, but only one active O-DU. 
The management system, SMO, must know and coordinate and ensure 
that there is only one active O-DU. 
 
Step 4.7 (ALT) 
STANDBY ODU BECOMES ACTIVE  
 
The forme rly standby O -DU#2 now becomes the active O -DU for the 
Shared O-RU. 
 
Note: there are preconditions that are relevant and necessary for this to 
happen. It is necessary that a call home between the ORU and standby 
ODU, and the replication of the configuratio n information has occurred 
and that the standby O-DU has the configuration of the active O-DU.  
 
Step 4.8 (ALT) 
CONFIGURATION FROM NEW ACTIVE O-DU 
 
The newly active O -DU may perform connectivity or configuration 
operations as it becomes the new active O-DU.  
Note: The new active O-DU has control only of its carriers. It will not have 
control of ALD devices. 
 
Step 5.1 (ALT) 
CU-PLANE MONITORING  
 
In the Shared O -RU, when CU Plane Monitoring interval timer triggers, 
the Shared O -RU will detect that is has lost CU logical plane is lost or 
payload is lost. 
 
Conditional – only carriers running, and only those carriers generate 
alarms. Lack of carrier traffic generates the alarms. 
 
 
Step 5.2 (ALT) 
O-RU RAISES ALARMS TO SUBSCRIBERS 
 
The Shared O -RU raises the M -Plane loss connectivity alarm to 
Subscriber(s). The simple case shows that the O-DU#1 and O-DU#2 are 
subscribers. 
 
Step 5.3 (ALT) O-RU RAISES ALARMS TO SUBSCRIBERS  

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
© 2023 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the copyright statement on the cover page of this specification.         157 
O-RAN.WG1.Use-Cases-Detailed-Specification-R003-v10.00 
 
The Shared O -RU raises the M -Plane loss connectivity alarm to 
Subscriber(s). The simple case shows that the O-DU#1 and O-DU#2 are 
subscribers. The Shared O-RU Raises an alarm to subscribers (O-DUs) 
that are still active, connected and subscribed. 
 
Step 5.4 (ALT) 
ALARM FORWARDED 
 
The Shared O-RU alarm is forwarded to the managing entity, such as the 
SMO. It is possible that the SMO will make the decision for making the 
standby O-DU#2 into the active O-DU.  
 
Note: There are many possible variations of this use case, where the 
SMO directly makes the decision of whether to make a standby O -DU 
into an active O-DU. This may happen even without a failure. These will 
be documented in other Sub-use cases. 
 
 
Step 5.5 (ALT) 
MANAGEMENT SYSTEM MAKES STANDBY ODU ACTIVE 
 
The Management system, SMO makes the standby O -DU#2 now 
becomes the active O-DU for the Shared O -RU. The message from the 
management system, SMO is sent to operational O-DU. 
 
Note: There might be multiple standby O-DUs, but only one active O-DU. 
The management system, SMO, must know and coordinate and ensure 
that there is only one active O-DU. 
 
Step 5.6 (ALT) 
STANDBY ODU BECOMES ACTIVE  
 
The formerly standby O -DU#2 now becomes the active O -DU for the 
Shared O-RU. 
 
Note: there are preconditions that are relevant and necessary for this to 
happen. It is necessary that a call home between the ORU and standby 
ODU, and the replication of the configuration information has occurred 
and that the standby O-DU has the configuration of the active O-DU.  
 
Step 5.7 (ALT) 
CONFIGURATION FROM NEW ACTIVE O-DU 
 
The newly active O -DU may perform connectivity or configuration 
operations as it becomes the new active O-DU.  
Note: The new active O-DU has control only of its carriers. It will not have 
control of ALD devices. 
 
Ends when The Use Case ends when the standby O-DU, O-DU #2 shown in the flow 
diagram has taken over for the previously active O-DU, O-DU #1.  
Exceptions 
There are many possible exceptions. Some of these include: 
If the Shared O-RU fails during a switch over 
If the Standby O -DU #2 also becomes unavailable when it is due to 
become active. 
If any event messaging for the flow is lost 
If configuration was not done properly 
If the Standby O-DU losses the configuration data from the configuration 
replica. 
If the Active O-DU returns to service while the Standby O-DU is trying to 
become the active O-DU. 
If the connectivity, or functionality of the management system (SMO) 
becomes unavailable.  
 
Post Conditions 
SUCCESSFUL POST-CONDITION – On a successful post-condition, the 
Shared O-RU is connected to the newly active O-DU, the newly active O-
DU is operational and has properly synced with the O-RU. 
 
FAILURE POST -CONDITION – If one of the various exception cases 
occurs, ther e are a variety of failure post conditions. If no O -DUs are 
available and the O -RU is orphaned no service is available and the O -
RU should shut down operations. If misconfiguration occurs the O-RU will 
respond accordingly. If there are ever two active O -DUs, the shared O -
RU will operate accordingly.

3.20.3.11 Reset use case of a shared O-RU 1 
The following will describe the solution for the reset sub use case for a Shared O-RU. 2 
Use Case Stage Evolution / Specification <<Uses>> 
Related use  
Goal 
The goal of this sub use case is to describe the flow related to reset of 
Shared O-RU for a Single MNO Operator configuration. 
 
This is a service impacting use case. 
 
Actors and 
Roles 
Shared O-RU 
The Shared O-RU is a key actor. It undergoes reset in this use case. 
The Shared O -RU may be reset by intention / request or 
autonomously. 
O-DUs (Host/Tenant/ &other O-DUs) 
All the O -DUs connected to the Shared O -RU are actors are 
involved in the reset operation. O-DU#1 has the role of the Shared 
O-RU Host, it also has a role of Shared Resource Operator (SRO). 
O-DU#2 is only a SRO. 
SMO: 
The SMO is informed by the O -DU that O -RU has been reset or 
issues a reset. 
 
Assumptions 
It is assumed that there is always at least one O-DU still operational 
with the Shared O-RU. 
 
This use case describes the flow for a Single MNO Operator 
configuration. 
 
 
Begins when 
The reset of a Shared O-RU use case may be invoked when there is a 
direct request to reset the Shared O-RU or it may be reset 
autonomously. 
 
There are many possible reasons why a Shared O-RU may need to be 
intentionally reset. Maintenance, software upgrade, network failure, 
power outages, communication link issues are just some of the many 
possible situations where the active O-RU would be reset. 
 
Preconditions 
The shared O-RU has connectivity to one or more O-DUs (and one of 
them is serving the primary role). 
The Shared O-DU has been configured originally by the active O-DU, 
and also carriers for the standby O-DUs. 
O-DUs have subscribed to alarm notifications successfully. 
 
Step 1 (M) 
[SHARED O-RU RESET FLOW] 
RESET REQUEST FROM SMO 
 
A reset request is communicated from the SMO to the Shared O-RU 
Host (O-DU #1). The reset request may be originated from the SMO for 
a variety of reasons. 
 
 
Step 2 (M) 
RESET REQUEST FROM O-DU 
 
The reset request is communicated onward from the Shared O-RU Host 
(O-DU #1) to the Shared O-RU through the open front-haul interface. 
 
 
Step 3 (M) 
RESET REPLY 
 
The Shared O-RU RPC Reply Acknowledge is sent from the Shared O-
RU to the Shared O-RU Host (O-DU #1). 
 
 
Step 4 (M) 
SHARED O-RU RESET 
 
Once invoked, the Shared O-RU goes through its reset sequence to 
complete the reset operation. 
 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
© 2023 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the copyright statement on the cover page of this specification.         162 
O-RAN.WG1.Use-Cases-Detailed-Specification-R003-v10.00 
 
Step 5 (M) 
RESET RESPONSE 
 
The Shared O-RU Host (O-DU #1) informs the SMO with a reset 
response 
 
 
Step 6 (M) 
[AUTONOMOUS RESET FLOW] 
 
AUTONOMOUS SHARED O-RU RESET 
 
The Shared O-RU is Autonomously Reset. 
 
 
Step 7 (M) 
O-DU INITIAL DETECTS LOSS OF CONNECTION 
 
The Shared O-DU Host (O-DU #1) detects Loss of polling as a result of 
the autonomous O-RU reset. It may also detect a Call Home Signal 
from a Shared O-RU that just had a valid M-Plane session.  
 
 
Step 8 (M) 
O-DU DETERMINES LOSS OF CONNECTION 
 
The O-DU can deduce that O-RU has a lost connection with broken 
polling with the O-DU. The O-DU does not know if the O-RU was 
performing a reset or if there was other reason for the lost connection, 
for example, a broken optical fiber. The O-DU can only report lost 
connection to O-RU in such a case. 
 
The O-DU redetects the Shared O-RU through a Call home from the 
Shared O-RU. Then the Shared O-RU Start up sequence of that Sub 
Use Case happens (see the ref flow). Afterwards, the O-DU can read 
the reset cause from the Shared O-RU. 
 
Step 9 (M) 
O-DU INFORMS SMO 
 
When the O-DU #1 starts sensing Call Home signals from O-RU, O-DU 
can deduce that O-RU has returns to service after a reset. Afterwards, 
the O-DU #1 can read the restart cause. Then, the Shared O-DU host 
can report to SMO that O-RU is re-detected and what was the reason 
why the O-RU reset. Then O-DU can fill update its aggregated model 
with details obtained from the O-RU and populate this information to 
SMO. 
 
Step 14 When O-DU redetects, the SMO can clear the alarm 
 
 
Ends when 
The Use Case ends the Shared O -RU has reset whether by reset or by 
autonomous reset. 
 
 
Exceptions 
There are many possible exceptions. Some of these include: 
The Shared O-RU was not able to successfully reset. 
The O-DU #1 was not able to properly detect lost connection with the 
Shared O-RU through loss of polling or call home signal was never sent. 
The O-DU #1 was not able to establish a restore connection to the Shared 
O-RU after reset. 
 
 
Post Conditions 
SUCCESSFUL POST-CONDITION – On a successful post-condition, the 
Shared O-RU is reset, and has restored connectivity to the Shared O-RU 
Host (O-DU #1). 
 
FAILURE POST-CONDITION – One of the failure exceptions has been 
encountered.

3.20.3.12 Advanced Resiliency Sub-use cases of a shared O-RU 1 
Advanced Resiliency Sub Use Cases describes other more intricate interactions and response for Resiliency operations.  2 
3.20.3.13 Load-Balancing Sub-use cases of a shared O-RU 3 
The Load-balancing Sub Use Cases describes the flow of how actors involved execute a policy to load -balance the 4 
resources of the O-DUs and Shared O-RU coordinated through a policy enforcer (actor). 5 
3.20.4 Required data 6 
3.20.4.1 Required data for all Shared O-RU Use Cases 7 
The following required data is relevant to the following sub use cases: Resource partitioning, Start-up, Configuration, 8 
Supervision, Performance Management, ALD control, Antenna Calibration, Rehoming, and Shutdown: 9 
 Inventory system maintains inventory data for the Shared O-RUs because it needs to be able to identify shared 10 
O-RUs. 11 
 The resource partitioning rApp maintains carrier resource information because it needs to be able to partition 12 
the shared O-RU carrier resources between different O-DU nodes.  13 
 In hierarchical management mode, the configuration rApp maintains the active/standby state & status  for O-14 
DUs because needs to determine which O-DU is responsible for configuring the common aspects of a shared O-15 
RU. 16 
 The supervision needs to include the O-DU identity  because the s hared O -RU needs to be able to support 17 
supervision on a per O-DU basis. 18 
 Alarm data  needs to be kept at the Shared O -RU because the Shared O -RU needs to be able to terminate 19 
transmissions associated with an O-DU when it loses supervision with that O-DU and to continue to operate with 20 
other O-DUs. There will be a history of Alarm data. 21 
 Shared O-RU measurement counters and KPIs (as defined by O -RAN M-Plane Spec) should be available on a 22 
per O-DU basis. 23 
 O-DU needs to include its O-DU identity to enable supervision operation on a per O-DU basis. 24 
 The ALD control rApp maintains data to keep track which O-DU is responsible for ALD controller functionality 25 
because it needs to be able to select which O-DU is responsible for ALD controller functionality. 26

MNO.  30

3.21 Use case 21: Energy Saving 21 
This section provides the motivations, descriptions, and proposed solutions for different Energy Efficie ncy and Energy 22 
Saving features (sub use cases). While there are energy savings by improving base station hardware efficiency and by the 23 
evolution of radio access technologies, the EE/ES use case primarily addresses enhancements in software efficiency and 24 
optimized configuration/control of various elements and functions, which are often AI/ML based.  25 
3.21.1 Background and goal of the use case 26 
The RAN is responsible for a major part of the Energy Consumption (EC) of a mobile network, and the O -RU accounts 27 
for the largest part of the energy consumption of the RAN. The rarefication of fossil fuel -based energy resources and the 28 
urgent need to reduce CO2 emissions make the EC a strategic topic for network operators, in addition of being a significant 29 
component of the operators’ OPEX.  30 
EC can be reduced by improving the Energy Efficiency (EE) of the network, and by introducing different Energy Saving 31 
(ES) mechanisms. Several ES mechanisms are related to switching off certain components in the network and differ from 32 
one another by their scope, time scale and network area. Applicable ES methods are for instance strongly load dependent. 33 
Optimization efficiency might be further improved by AI/ML based configuration thereof.  34 
RAN functions related to network energy saving solutions have been studied in 3GPP RAN3 in Rel.17 as part of the 35 
Study on Enhancement for Data Collection for NR and EN -DC. The outcome is do cumented in 3GPP TR 37.817  [15]. 36 
3GPP RAN2 and RAN3 might specify enhancements for the Minimization of Drive Tests (MDT) procedures and/or 37 
signaling procedures tha t rely on Xn signaling in Rel.18. While 3GPP RAN WGs work on solutions with ML model 38 
inference within the gNB, O -RAN specifies solutions that benefit from ML model inference in the Near -RT or Non-RT 39 
RIC (e.g., optimizing the network in larger service areas ). For EE related network management 3GPP SA5 defined use 40 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
© 2023 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the copyright statement on the cover page of this specification.         168 
O-RAN.WG1.Use-Cases-Detailed-Specification-R003-v10.00 
cases, requirements, and solutions in 3GPP TS 28.310  [4]. Furthermore, EC measurements and KPIs for 5G net works, 1 
Network Functions, NG -RAN and gNBs such as Energy Efficiency and Energy Consumption KPIs and performance 2 
measurements are defined in 3GPP TS 28.554 [8]. Centralized and Distributed ES Management Functions are defined in 3 
3GPP TS 28.541 [6].   4 
EE can be considered for the whole network (i.e. , end-to-end), for a sub-network or per single network element. Within 5 
a network element it could be applicable per specific radio resource management mechanism or per radio or transport 6 
network link. Network wise EE is defined as the ratio between the data volume delivered in the network and the network 7 
EC observed during the time -period required to deliver such data, with possible adaptations to account for different 8 
deployment scenarios and load situations (ETS ES 203 228 [22], 3GPP TR 38.913 [19]). 3GPP has launched a study item 9 
within Rel-18 (RP-213554: “Study on network energy saving for NR”) that will  include among others, an evaluation 10 
methodology and KPIs for EC and ES gains and their impact on network and UE performance and EE. To assess EE and 11 
ES associated to radio resource management mechanisms and links, appropriate KPIs are necessary.   12 
In a timescale of minutes, hours and above, and when the cell load is low, ES can be achieved by switching off one or 13 
more carriers or the cell. In a timescale from seconds to minutes, ES can be achieved by switching off RF channels 14 
(including possibly antennas) of a Massive MIMO system. Tx and Rx parts might be switched independently. In a very 15 
short timescale corresponding to a symbol, subframe or frame, Advanced Sleep Modes (ASM) can be considered. RF 16 
channel on/off switching can be used at medium load and ASM might be usable even at high load. Lastly, ES solutions 17 
can be applied to the O-Cloud, namely to the O-CU and O-DU, and can cover mechanisms such as scale in/out processes, 18 
workload placement or hardware processors’ sleep modes etc. AI/ML is useful for all  the above mechanisms with the 19 
important role of determining the switch off/on time that maximizes ES gain. 20

3.21.3 Solutions 28 
Editor’s note: Sub use case specific solutions with detailed descriptions in fully separate sections.  29 
3.21.3.1 Carrier and Cell switch off/on 30 
Mobile networks often utilize multiple frequency layers (carriers) to cover the same service area. At low load, ES can be 31 
achieved by switching off one or more carriers or entire cell s without impairing the network performance . The switch 32 
off/on decision c an be made by an AI/ML model within the inference host , deployed at the Non -RT RIC (deployment 33 
option 1) or at the Near -RT RIC (deployment option 2), as described above. Among others, the AI/ML models' 34 
functionality may include prediction of future traffic , user mobility, and resource usage and may also predict expected 35 
energy efficiency enhancements, resource usage, and network performance for different ES optimization states. Before 36 
switching off/on carrier(s) or cell(s), the E2 Node may need to perform s ome preparation actions for off switching (e.g., 37 
to enable, disable, modify Carrier Aggregation and/or Dual Connectivity, to trigger HO traffic and UEs from cells/carriers 38 
to other cells or carriers , informing neighboring nodes via X2/Xn interface etc.) as  well as for on switching (e.g., cell 39 
probing, informing neighboring nodes via X2/Xn interface etc.).  40

Use Case Stage Evolution / Specification <<Uses>> 
Related use  
Goal 
Enable Carrier and Cell switch off/on Energy Saving functions in the 
Network by means of configuration parameter change and Actions 
controlled by Non-RT RIC and allow for AI/ML-based solutions. 
 
Actors and Roles Non-RT RIC acting as Energy Saving decision making function. 
E2 Node and O-RU acting as configuration enforcement function.  
Assumptions 
O1 interface connectivity is established towards E2 Nodes, Non-RT RIC 
and SMO. 
Open FH M-Plane interface is established between E2 node and O -RU 
and/or SMO and O-RU directly.  
Network is operational. 
 
Pre-conditions Operator has set the targets for Energy Saving functions in the Non-RT 
RIC.  
Begins when  
Operator enables the optimization functions for carrier and cell switch 
off/on Energy Saving functions and E2 Node and O -RU become 
operational. 
 
Step 1 (M) SMO initiates specific measurement data collection request towards E2 
Node and O-RU for AI/ML model training and inference.   
Step 2 (M) E2 Node and O -RU send the configured measurement data to SMO 
periodically or event based.   
Step 3 (M) Non-RT RIC retrieves the collected measurement data for processing.  
Step 4 (M) 
Non-RT RIC trains the AI/ML model s with the collected data. Trained 
AI/ML models are deployed, configured, and activated. 
 
Non-RT RIC constantly monitors  
(i) performance and energy consumption of the E2 Node(s) 
(ii) energy consumption of O-RU(s) 
 
Step 5 (M) Based on the AI/ML inference the Non-RT RIC may request the SMO to 
configure E2 Node to prepare and execute cell or carrier switch off/on.  
Step 6 (M) 
SMO instructs E2 node via O1 interface to perform the received 
request(s) from the Non -RT RIC. O-RU is informed about the updated 
O-RU configuration via Open FH M-Plane interface either by E2 Node, 
or by SMO directly. E2 Node / O-RU will notify SMO once cell or carrier 
switch off/on is completed. 
 
Step 7 (M) 
Non-RT RIC continuously analyzes performance of AI/ML model. If 
energy saving objectives  are not achieved, it may decide to initiate 
fallback mechanism, and/or AI/ML model update or retraining.  
 
Ends when E2 Node becomes non -operational or when the operator disables the 
optimization functions for Energy Saving.  
Exceptions None.  
Post Conditions 
Non-RT RIC continues close loop monitoring of Energy Saving function 
at E2 Node and O-RU. 
E2 Node(s) and O -RU(s) operate using the newly deployed 
parameters/models and state (off/on).

3.22 Use case 22: MU-MIMO Optimizaiton 9 
This use case provides the motivation, description, and requirements for a near real time MU-MIMO optimization control 10 
loop deployment. Deploying MU -MIMO application in the Near -RT RIC enables new solutions that may optimize UE 11 
and cell level performance in certain deployments by e.g. deriving channel estimation/prediction and UEs selections with 12 
their associated precoding coefficients, resulting in increased per UE and overall cell throughput.  13 
3.22.1 Background and goal of the use case 14 
MU-MIMO is one of the key technologies available for increasing UE and cell capacities using existing time/frequency 15 
resources. The use of multiple antennas enables the pointing of beams to multiple UEs with each beam spatially filtering 16 
the interference from the other beams. This has the potential to provide higher total cell capacity when there are multiple 17 
eNB/gNB antennas. 18 
In a commercial deployment, some subscribers can be stationary, some can be pedestrian moving slowly, and some can 19 
be moving at high speed. Traditional MU-MIMO solutions are very sensitive to subscriber’s mobility and as a result the 20 
capacity gains achieved with multiple antennas is limited. 21 
New beamforming solutions are emerging that support MU -MIMO with less time sensitivity allowing them to be 22 
implemented in the Near-RT RIC. These solutions are applicable to both downlink and uplink data channels and to TDD 23 
as well as FDD and may provide high user and cell performance for subscribers moving within a wide range of speeds.  24 
The objective of this use case i s to allow the operator to improve user throughput and overall cell capacity by deploying 25 
an application in the Near-RT RIC that can use information collected from the E2 Nodes to calculate and send to the E2 26 
Nodes user selections and applicable precoding coefficients in a near real time loop. This use case will also open the door 27 
for future expansion of the MU-MIMO to supporting CoMP covering both ICIC and joint multi sites MU -MIMO. 28 
3.22.2 Entities/resources involved in the use case 29 
1) Near-RT RIC  30 
a) Retrieve cell configuration and UE states from E2 nodes 31 
b) Send configurations for DL channel estimation reporting and UL SRS and DMRS to the E2 nodes  32 
c) Retrieve DL/UL traffic, and DL/UL channel quality information from E2 nodes  33 
d) Use the retrieved information to select t he UEs to be spatially multiplexed per frequency and time resources 34 
and for each selection calculate the relevant MCS and precoder coefficients for optimal UE and cell throughput 35 
e) Send the recommended UE selections with their resource assignments, MCS, and precoding coefficients to the 36 
E2 nodes. 37 
2) E2 nodes  38 
a) Collect and report to Near -RT RIC information related to cell configuration, UE states, DL/UL traffic, and 39 
DL/UL channel quality.  40 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
© 2023 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the copyright statement on the cover page of this specification.         177 
O-RAN.WG1.Use-Cases-Detailed-Specification-R003-v10.00 
b) Apply the configurations received from the Near -RT RIC for DL channel estim ation reporting and UL SRS 1 
transmissions 2 
c) Apply MU-MIMO parameters following Near -RT RIC recommendations (while handling time critical events 3 
separately). 4 
3.22.3 Solutions 5 
3.22.3.1 MU-MIMO Optimization 6 
Use Case Stage Evolution / Specification <<Uses>> 
Related use  
Goal MU-MIMO optimization using Near-RT RIC control loop.  
Actors and Roles 
Near-RT RIC: configures E2 nodes’ measurements, collects data from 
E2 Nodes, performs MU-MIMO optimization function, and sends MIMO 
recommendations to E2 nodes. 
E2 Nodes: Report measurements to Near -RT RIC and execute MU -
MIMO recommendations. 
 
Assumptions E2 connectivity is established between Near -RT RIC and E2 Nodes. 
Network is operational.  
Pre conditions 
All relevant functions and components are instantiated. M U-MIMO 
Optimization xApp is deployed with initial configuration 
All relevant subscriptions established on E2 interface 
 
Begins when  Preconditions are met.  
Step 1 (M) 
Near-RT RIC initiates data collection from E2 Nodes (cell configuration, 
UE states, RRC connection, UL/DL traffic and channel information)  
Step 2 (M) 
E2 Nodes send cell configuration, UE states, and RRC connection 
information to Near-RT RIC.  
Step 3 (M) E2 nodes send UL/DL traffic and channel information to Near-RT RIC.  
Step 4 (O) 
Near-RT RIC sends DL channel estimation reporting and UL SRS and 
DMRS configuration to E2 Nodes.  
Step 5 (M) 
E2 nodes continuously send UL/DL traffic and channel information to 
Near-RT RIC.  
Step 6 (M) 
E2 nodes send updated UE states and RRC connections information to 
Near-RT RIC.  
Step 7 (M) 
Near-RT RIC uses the collected information to estimate channels and 
select UE groupings per ranges of frequency and time resources  
Step 8 (M) 
Near-RT RIC calculates MCS and precoding coefficients for each 
selection of UEs  
Step 9 (M) 
Near-RT RIC sends optimized MU -MIMO parameters (UE selections 
with their resource assignments, MCS, and precoding coefficients) to E2 
Nodes.  
Step 10 (M) E2 nodes schedule MU -MIMO transmissions using the parameters 
received from the Near-RT RIC   
Step 11 (O) Near-RT RIC sends updated DL channel estimation reporting and UL 
SRS and DMRS configuration to E2 Nodes.  
Ends when Operator uninstalls MU-MIMO Optimization xApp  
Exceptions FFS  
Post Conditions The E2 Nodes operate using the newly received parameters.

3.22.4 Required data 3 
The Near-RT RIC requires different types of data from the E2 Nodes as summarized below with examples : 4 
1) Cell configuration information (e.g., frequency and BW, FDD/TDD, SCS, UL-DL configuration) 5 
2) List of connected UEs 6 
3) UE connection updates (setup, release, handover) 7 
4) UE RRC state changes (connected, inactive, idle) 8 
5) UL channel information (e.g., SRS, ACK/NACK counts) 9 
6) DL channel information (e.g., CQI, RI, PMI, ACK/NACK counts) 10 
7) DL PDCP and RLC buffer status and UL BSR 11

Annex A (informative): Additional Information 1 
A.1 Traffic Steering use case A1 interface usage example 2 
Note: Please refer to WG2 Use Cases and Requirements Specification for more details and up to date definitions of this 3 
use case A1 interface usage examples. 4 
An example scenario is here used to describe the use of A1 for traffic steering, implying the Non-RT RIC sending policies 5 
for allocation of the control plane (RRC) and the user plane for different services, identified by their 5QI. 6 
In the scenario a UE with UEid=1, belonging to a subnet slice identified by S -NSSAI=1, having a Voice (5QI=1) and an 7 
MBB (5QI=9) connection established, enters an area covered by four frequency bands. The Non-RT RIC understands the 8 
requirements and characteristics of the services and decides to let the Voice and RRC connection reside on the low band 9 
(here covered by a macro cell B becoming the PCell), while the MBB connection should preferably use the higher band 10 
(here provided by a smaller cell C and D becoming the SCells) and avoid the low band if possible. Cell A is used for 11 
MBB if required for coverage reasons. 12 
Policies are sent to any cell of concern, e.g. where the UE resides and may move.  13 
 14 
Figure A.1-1 Desired use of the cells 15 
Two policies over A1 are needed to accomplish the desired behavior, described in JSON format below. Note that as part 16 
of the scope, the cell_id is optional, and if omitted it is up to the Near-RT RIC to locate the UE and there enforce the 17 
policy. 18 
{ 19 
    "policy_id": "1", 20 
    "scope": { 21 
      "ue_id": "1", 22 
      "slice_id": "1", 23 
      "qos_id": "1", 24 
  “cell_id”: ”X” // Policy for Cell X, where X is one of A, B, C or D 25 
    }, 26 
    "statement": { 27 
      "cell_id_list": "B", 28 
      "preference": "Shall", 29 
      "primary": true // Control plane on Cell B (becoming PCell) 30
